   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Australia Day</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub">
     <div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint">
      <div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic">

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Australian national holiday
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <table class="infobox vevent">

      <p><b>Australia Day</b> is the official <a href="/wiki/National_day" title="National day">national day</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. Observed annually on 26 January, it marks the 1788 landing of the <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">First Fleet</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cove" title="Sydney Cove">Sydney Cove</a> and raising of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Flag</a> by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Phillip" title="Arthur Phillip">Arthur Phillip</a> following days of exploration of <a href="/wiki/Port_Jackson" title="Port Jackson">Port Jackson</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>. In present-day Australia, celebrations aim to reflect the diverse society and landscape of the nation and are marked by community and family events, reflections on <a href="/wiki/Australian_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian history">Australian history</a>, official community awards and citizenship ceremonies welcoming new members of the Australian community.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The meaning and significance of Australia Day has evolved and been contested over time, and not all states have celebrated the same date as their date of historical significance.<sup id="cite_ref-Conversation_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conversation-2">[2]</a></sup> Unofficially, or historically, the date has also been variously named <b>Anniversary Day</b>, <b>Foundation Day</b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Australian_Natives%27_Association" title="Australian Natives' Association">ANA</a> Day</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The date of 26 January 1788 marked the proclamation of British sovereignty over the eastern seaboard of Australia (then known as <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">New Holland</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Although it was not known as Australia Day until over a century later, records of celebrations on 26 January date back to 1808, with the first official celebration of the formation of New South Wales held in 1818. On New Year's Day 1901, the British colonies of Australia formed a <a href="/wiki/Australian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Federation">federation</a>, marking the birth of modern Australia. A national day of unity and celebration was looked for. It was not until 1935 that all Australian states and territories adopted use of the term "Australia Day" to mark the date, and not until 1994 that the date was consistently marked by a public holiday on that day by all states and territories.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In contemporary Australia, the holiday is marked by the presentation of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_of_the_Year" title="Australian of the Year">Australian of the Year</a> Awards on Australia Day Eve, announcement of the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Day_Honours" class="mw-redirect" title="Australia Day Honours">Australia Day Honours</a> list and addresses from the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">governor-general</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">prime minister</a>. It is an official public holiday in every state and territory. With community festivals, concerts and citizenship ceremonies, the day is celebrated in large and small communities and cities around the nation. Australia Day has become the biggest annual civic event in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australian</a> events are now included. However, since at least 1938,<sup id="cite_ref-Age09_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Age09-7">[7]</a></sup> the date of Australia Day has also been marked by Indigenous Australians and supporters mourning what is seen as the invasion of the land by the British and the start of <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation of Australia">colonisation</a>, protesting its celebration as a national holiday. 26 January is referred to as <b>Invasion Day</b>, <b>Survival Day</b>, or <b>Day of Mourning</b> and observed as a <a href="/wiki/Counter-celebration" title="Counter-celebration">counter-observance</a>, with calls for the date to be changed,<sup id="cite_ref-nitv2016_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nitv2016-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_2017-01-26_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_2017-01-26-9">[9]</a></sup> or the holiday to be abolished entirely.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> However, support for changing the date has remained a minority position.<sup id="cite_ref-Ipsos_2021_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ipsos_2021-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
