      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_the_First_Fleet">Arrival of the First Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Arrival of the First Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">First Fleet</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 13 May 1787 a fleet of 11 ships, which came to be known as the First Fleet, was sent by the <a href="/wiki/British_Admiralty" class="mw-redirect" title="British Admiralty">British Admiralty</a> from England to New Holland. Under the command of Naval Captain Arthur Phillip, the fleet sought to establish a <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal colony</a> at <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a> on the coast of New South Wales, which had been explored and <a href="/wiki/Possession_Island,_Queensland" class="mw-redirect" title="Possession Island, Queensland">claimed</a> by Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> in 1770. The settlement was seen as necessary because of the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The Fleet arrived between 18 and 20 January 1788, but it was immediately apparent that Botany Bay was unsuitable. </p>
      <p>On 21 January, Phillip and a few officers travelled to Port Jackson, 12 kilometres (7.5&nbsp;mi) to the north, to see if it would be a better location for a settlement. They stayed there until 23 January; Phillip named the site of their landing Sydney Cove, after the Home Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Townshend,_1st_Viscount_Sydney" title="Thomas Townshend, 1st Viscount Sydney">Thomas Townshend, 1st Viscount Sydney</a>. They also made contact with the local Aboriginal people. </p>
      <p>They returned to Botany Bay on the evening of 23 January, when Phillip gave orders to move the fleet to Sydney Cove the next morning, 24 January. That day, there was a huge gale blowing, making it impossible to leave Botany Bay, so they decided to wait till the next day, 25 January. However, during 24 January, they spotted the ships <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Astrolabe_(1781)" title="French ship Astrolabe (1781)">Astrolabe</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Boussole_(1781)" title="French ship Boussole (1781)">Boussole</a></i>, flying the French flag, at the entrance to Botany Bay; they were having as much trouble getting into the bay as the First Fleet was having getting out.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>On 25 January the gale was still blowing; the fleet tried to leave Botany Bay, but only <a href="/wiki/HMS_Supply_(1759)" title="HMS Supply (1759)">HMS&nbsp;<i>Supply</i></a> made it out, carrying Arthur Phillip, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Gidley_King" title="Philip Gidley King">Philip Gidley King</a>, some marines and about 40 convicts; they anchored in Sydney Cove in the afternoon. Meanwhile, back at Botany Bay, Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Hunter_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="John Hunter (Royal Navy officer)">John Hunter</a> of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Sirius_(1786)" title="HMS Sirius (1786)">HMS&nbsp;<i>Sirius</i></a> made contact with the French ships, and he and the commander, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Sutton_de_Clonard" title="Robert Sutton de Clonard">Captain de Clonard</a>, exchanged greetings. Clonard informed Hunter that the fleet commander was <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Galaup,_comte_de_La_P%C3%A9rouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-François de Galaup, comte de La Pérouse">Jean-François de Galaup, comte de La Pérouse</a>. <i>Sirius</i> successfully cleared Botany Bay, but the other ships were in great difficulty. <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_(1784_ship)" title="Charlotte (1784 ship)"><i>Charlotte</i></a> was blown dangerously close to rocks; <i><a href="/wiki/Friendship_(ship)" title="Friendship (ship)">Friendship</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_(1786_ship)" title="Prince of Wales (1786 ship)"><i>Prince of Wales</i></a> became entangled, both ships losing booms or sails; <i>Charlotte</i> and the <i>Friendship</i> actually collided; and <a href="/wiki/Lady_Penrhyn_(1786_ship)" title="Lady Penrhyn (1786 ship)"><i>Lady Penrhyn</i></a> nearly ran aground. Despite these difficulties, all the remaining ships finally managed to clear Botany Bay and sail to Sydney Cove on 26 January. The last ship anchored there at about 3&nbsp;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove,_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/220px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/330px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/440px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3433" data-file-height="2500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove,_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Capt. Arthur Phillip raising the British flag at Sydney Cove, 26 January 1788. Oil sketch by <a href="/wiki/Algernon_Talmage" title="Algernon Talmage">Algernon Talmage</a>, 1937.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day_plaque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Australia_Day_plaque.jpg/220px-Australia_Day_plaque.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Australia_Day_plaque.jpg/330px-Australia_Day_plaque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Australia_Day_plaque.jpg/440px-Australia_Day_plaque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day_plaque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Foundation of Australia plaque, Loftus Street, Circular Quay
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> So it was on 26 January that a landing was made at Sydney Cove and clearing of the ground for an encampment immediately began. Then, according to Phillip's account:<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>In the evening of the 26th the colours were displayed on shore, and the Governor, with several of his principal officers and others, assembled round the flag-staff, drank the king's health, and success to the settlement, with all that display of form which on such occasions is esteemed propitious, because it enlivens the spirits, and fills the imagination with pleasing presages.</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite>The Voyage of Governor Phillip to Botany Bay</cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>The formal establishment of the Colony of New South Wales did not however occur on 26 January as is commonly assumed. It did not occur until 7 February 1788, when the formal proclamation of the colony and of Arthur Phillip's governorship were read out. The vesting of all land in the reigning monarch <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a> also dates from 7 February 1788.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_fifty_years:_1788_to_1838">First fifty years: 1788 to 1838</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First fifty years: 1788 to 1838">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Although there was no official recognition of the colony's anniversary, with the <i>New South Wales Almanacks</i> of 1806 and 1808 placing no special significance on 26 January,<sup id="cite_ref-Bonyhady2003p42_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonyhady2003p42-21">[21]</a></sup> by 1808 the date was being used by the colony's immigrants, especially the <a href="/wiki/Emancipist" title="Emancipist">emancipated convicts</a>, to "celebrate their love of the land they lived in"<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> with "drinking and merriment".<sup id="cite_ref-ClarkAustraliaDayHistory_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClarkAustraliaDayHistory-23">[23]</a></sup> The 1808 celebrations followed this pattern, beginning at sunset on 25 January and lasting into the night, the chief toast of the occasion being <a href="/wiki/George_Johnston_(New_South_Wales)" class="mw-redirect" title="George Johnston (New South Wales)">Major George Johnston</a>. Johnston had the honour of being the first officer ashore from the First Fleet, having been carried from the landing boat on the back of convict <a href="/wiki/James_Ruse" title="James Ruse">James Ruse</a>. Despite suffering the ill-effects of a fall from his gig on the way home to <a href="/wiki/Annandale,_New_South_Wales" title="Annandale, New South Wales">Annandale</a>, Johnston led the officers of the <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_Corps" title="New South Wales Corps">New South Wales Corps</a> in arresting Governor <a href="/wiki/William_Bligh" title="William Bligh">William Bligh</a> on the following day, 26 January 1808, in what became known as the "<a href="/wiki/Rum_Rebellion" title="Rum Rebellion">Rum Rebellion</a>". </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Almanac" title="Almanac">Almanacs</a> started mentioning "First Landing Day" or "Foundation Day" and successful immigrants started holding anniversary dinners.<sup id="cite_ref-Conversation_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conversation-2">[2]</a></sup> In 1817 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sydney_Gazette_and_New_South_Wales_Advertiser" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sydney Gazette and New South Wales Advertiser">The Sydney Gazette and New South Wales Advertiser</a></i> reported on one of these unofficial gatherings at the home of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Nichols" title="Isaac Nichols">Isaac Nichols</a>: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942">
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>On Monday the 27th ult. a dinner party met at the house of Mr. Isaac Nichols, for the purpose of celebrating the Anniversary of the Institution of this Colony under Governor Philip, which took place on 26 Jan. 1788, but this year happening upon a Sunday, the commemoration dinner was reserved for the day following. The party assembled were select, and about 40 in number. At 5 in the afternoon dinner was on the table, and a more agreeable entertainment could not have been anticipated. After dinner a number of loyal toasts were drank, and a number of festive songs given; and about 10 the company parted, well gratified with the pleasures that the meeting had afforded.</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite><i>The Sydney Gazette and New South Wales Advertiser</i><sup id="cite_ref-SydneyGazette1817-02-01_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyGazette1817-02-01-24">[24]</a></sup></cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>1818 was the 30th anniversary of the founding of the colony, and Governor <a href="/wiki/Lachlan_Macquarie" title="Lachlan Macquarie">Lachlan Macquarie</a> chose to acknowledge the day with the first official celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> The governor declared that the day would be a holiday for all government workers, granting each an extra allowance of "one pound [c. 450g] of fresh meat", and ordered a 30-gun salute at <a href="/wiki/Dawes_Point,_New_South_Wales" title="Dawes Point, New South Wales">Dawes Point</a> – one for each year that the colony had existed.<sup id="cite_ref-Watts1818-01-24_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watts1818-01-24-26">[26]</a></sup> This began a tradition that was retained by the Governors that were to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Regatta_1838_advertising_in_Sydney_Gazette.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sydney_Regatta_1838_advertising_in_Sydney_Gazette.jpg/220px-Sydney_Regatta_1838_advertising_in_Sydney_Gazette.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Sydney_Regatta_1838_advertising_in_Sydney_Gazette.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="207"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Regatta_1838_advertising_in_Sydney_Gazette.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The first in what would become the Sydney Regatta tradition, 26 January 1838.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Foundation Day, as it was known at the time, continued to be officially celebrated in New South Wales, and in doing so became connected with sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> One of these became a tradition that is still continued today: in 1837 the first running of what would become the Australia Day <a href="/wiki/Regatta" class="mw-redirect" title="Regatta">regatta</a> was held on <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydney Harbour">Sydney Harbour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SydneyGazette1837-01-28_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyGazette1837-01-28-27">[27]</a></sup> Five races were held for different classes of boats, from first class sailing vessels to <a href="/wiki/Watermen" class="mw-redirect" title="Watermen">watermen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Skiff" title="Skiff">skiffs</a>, and people viewed the festivities from both onshore and from the decks of boats on the harbour, including the <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steamboat</a> <i>Australian</i> and the <i>Francis Freeling</i>—the latter running aground during the festivities and having to be refloated the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-SydneyHeraldRegatta1837-01-30_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyHeraldRegatta1837-01-30-28">[28]</a></sup> Happy with the success of the regatta, the organisers resolved to make it an annual event.<sup id="cite_ref-SydneyGazette1837-01-28_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyGazette1837-01-28-27">[27]</a></sup> However, some of the celebrations had gained an air of elitism, with the "United Australians" dinner being limited to those born in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> In describing the dinner, the <i>Sydney Herald</i> justified the decision, saying: </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942">
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>The parties who associated themselves under the title of "United Australians" have been censured for adopting a principle of exclusiveness. It is not fair so to censure them. If they invited emigrants to join them they would give offence to another class of persons – while if they invited all they would be subject to the presence of persons with whom they might not wish to associate. That was a good reason. The "Australians" had a perfect right to dine together if they wished it, and no one has a right to complain.</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite><i>The Sydney Herald</i><sup id="cite_ref-SydneyHeraldDinner1837-01-30_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyHeraldDinner1837-01-30-29">[29]</a></sup></cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>The following year, 1838, was the 50th anniversary of the founding of the colony, and as part of the celebrations Australia's first public holiday was declared. The regatta was held for a second time, and people crowded the foreshores to view the events, or joined the five steamers (<i>Maitland</i>, <i>Experiment</i>, <i>Australia</i>, <i>Rapid</i>, and the miniature steamer <i>Firefly</i>) to view the proceedings from the water. At midday 50 guns were fired from Dawes' Battery as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Standard of the United Kingdom">Royal Standard</a> was raised, and in the evening rockets and other fireworks lit the sky.<sup id="cite_ref-SydneyHeraldJubilee1838-01-29_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyHeraldJubilee1838-01-29-30">[30]</a></sup> The dinner was a smaller affair than the previous year, with only 40 in attendance compared to the 160 from 1837,<sup id="cite_ref-SydneyHeraldDinner1837-01-30_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyHeraldDinner1837-01-30-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SydneyHeraldJubilee1838-01-29_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydneyHeraldJubilee1838-01-29-30">[30]</a></sup> and the anniversary as a whole was described as a "day for everyone".<sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centenary_celebration:_1839_to_1935">Centenary celebration: 1839 to 1935</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Centenary celebration: 1839 to 1935">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg/220px-100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg/330px-100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg/440px-100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="410"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:100th_Anniversary_of_Australia_settlement_banquent.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>NSW state banquet to commemorate "the first 100 years of Australian settlement", 26 January 1888
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Prior to 1888, 26 January was very much a New South Wales affair, as each of the colonies had its own commemoration for its founding. In Tasmania, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hobart_Regatta" title="Royal Hobart Regatta">Regatta Day</a> occurred initially in December to mark the anniversary of the landing of <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> South Australia celebrated <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_Day_(South_Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Proclamation Day (South Australia)">Proclamation Day</a> on 28 December. Western Australia had its own Foundation Day (now <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia_Day" title="Western Australia Day">Western Australia Day</a>) on 1 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The decision to mark the occasion of the First Fleet’s arrival in 1788 at Sydney Cove and Captain Arthur Phillip’s proclamation of British sovereignty over the eastern continent on January 26, was made by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Natives%27_Association" title="Australian Natives' Association">Australian Natives' Association</a> (ANA), a group of white "native-born" middle class men formed in Victoria in the late 1800s.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1888, all colonial capitals except <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a> celebrated "Anniversary Day". In 1910, South Australia adopted 26 January as "Foundation Day",<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> to replace another holiday known as Accession Day, which had been held on 22 January to mark the accession to the throne of <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="King Edward VII">King Edward VII</a>, who died in May 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-Adreview_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adreview-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Australia Day was established in response to Australia's involvement in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. In 1915, the mother of four <a href="/wiki/Servicemen" class="mw-redirect" title="Servicemen">servicemen</a> thought up the idea of a national day, with the specific aim of raising funds for wounded soldiers, and the term was coined to stir up patriotic feelings.<sup id="cite_ref-abcsensw_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcsensw-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Adreview_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adreview-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1915 a committee to celebrate Australia Day was formed, and the date chosen was 30 July,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> on which many fund-raising efforts were run to support the war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-TheOtherAustraliaDay_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheOtherAustraliaDay-36">[36]</a></sup> It was also held in July in subsequent years of World War I: on 28 July 1916,<sup id="cite_ref-TheOtherAustraliaDay_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheOtherAustraliaDay-36">[36]</a></sup> 27 July 1917,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and 26 July 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> adopted 26 January as Australia Day in 1931,<sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> and by 1935, all states of Australia were celebrating 26 January as Australia Day (although it was still known as Anniversary Day in New South Wales).<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> The name "Foundation Day" persisted in local usage.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sesquicentenary">Sesquicentenary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sesquicentenary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg/220px-Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg/330px-Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg/440px-Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg 2x" data-file-width="766" data-file-height="576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Federation_Sesqui-Centenary_celebrations_063992.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sesquicentenary parade in Sydney, 26 January 1938
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The 150th anniversary of British settlement in Australia in 1938 was widely celebrated.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> Preparations began in 1936 with the formation of a Celebrations Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> In that year, New South Wales was the only state to abandon the traditional long weekend, and the annual Anniversary Day public holiday was held on the actual anniversary day – Wednesday 26 January.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> The Commonwealth and state governments agreed to unify the celebrations on 26 January as "Australia Day" in 1946,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> although the public holiday was instead taken on the Monday closest to the actual anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-?NADCHistory_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-?NADCHistory-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicentennial_year">Bicentennial year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bicentennial year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg/220px-First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg/330px-First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg/440px-First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="373"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:First_Fleet_Reenactment_1988.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sydney Harbour, 26 January 1988
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_Bicentenary" title="Australian Bicentenary">Australian Bicentenary</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1988, the celebration of 200 years since the arrival of the First Fleet was organised on a large scale, with many significant events taking place in all major cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup> Over 2.5&nbsp;million people attended the event in Sydney.<sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> These included street parties, concerts, including performances on the steps and forecourt of the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Opera_House" title="Sydney Opera House">Sydney Opera House</a> and at many other public venues, art and literary competitions, historic re-enactments, and the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Powerhouse_Museum" title="Powerhouse Museum">Powerhouse Museum</a> at its new location. A <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet_Re-enactment_Voyage" title="First Fleet Re-enactment Voyage">re-enactment of the arrival of the First Fleet</a> took place in Sydney Harbour, with ships that had sailed from <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> a year earlier taking part.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwan_22-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwan-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nsw-hist_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsw-hist-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_celebrations">Contemporary celebrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contemporary celebrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Since 1988, participation in Australia Day has increased, and in 1994 all states and territories began to celebrate a unified public holiday on the actual day for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-history_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-42">[42]</a></sup> Previously, some states had celebrated the public holiday on a Monday or Friday to ensure a <a href="/wiki/Long_weekend" title="Long weekend">long weekend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kwan_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwan-43">[43]</a></sup> Research conducted in 2007 reported that 28% of Australians polled attended an organised Australia Day event and a further 26% celebrated with family and friends.<sup id="cite_ref-DeeryJagoFredline2007_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeeryJagoFredline2007-44">[44]</a></sup> This reflected the results of an earlier research project where 66% of respondents anticipated that they would actively celebrate Australia Day 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg/220px-Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg/330px-Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg/440px-Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1294" data-file-height="835"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lotto_Skyworks_Applecross.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>500,000 people watch the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Perth_Skyworks" title="City of Perth Skyworks">City of Perth Skyworks</a> at <a href="/wiki/Applecross,_Western_Australia" title="Applecross, Western Australia">Applecross, Western Australia</a> on Australia Day, 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Outdoor concerts, community barbecues, sports competitions, festivals and fireworks are some of the many events held in communities across Australia. These official events are presented by the <a href="/wiki/National_Australia_Day_Council" title="National Australia Day Council">National Australia Day Council</a>, an official council or committee in each state and territory, and local committees.<sup id="cite_ref-NADC2009Report_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NADC2009Report-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Sydney, the harbour is a focus and boat races are held, such as a ferry race and the tall ships race. In Adelaide, the key celebrations are "Australia Day in the City" which is a parade, concert and fireworks display held in Elder Park, with a new outdoor art installation in 2019 designed to acknowledge, remember and recognise Aboriginal people who have contributed to the community.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Featuring the People's March and the Voyages Concert, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>'s events<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> focus strongly on the celebration of multiculturalism.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Perth_Skyworks" title="City of Perth Skyworks">Perth Skyworks</a> is the largest single event presented each Australia Day.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_(5475800868).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg/220px-Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg/330px-Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg/440px-Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_%285475800868%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day_Citizenship_Ceremony_2011_(5475800868).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Prime Minister of Australia, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">Julia Gillard</a>, and the Department of Immigration and Citizenship Secretary, Andrew Metcalfe, hand out citizenship certificates to new Australian citizens (2011)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Citizenship ceremonies are also commonly held, with Australia Day now the largest occasion for the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Australian_nationality_law" title="Australian nationality law">Australian citizenship</a>. On 26 January 2011, more than 300 citizenship ceremonies took place and around 13,000 people from 143 countries took Australian citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In recent years many citizenship ceremonies have included an <a href="/wiki/Australian_citizenship_affirmation" title="Australian citizenship affirmation">affirmation</a> by existing citizens. Research conducted in 2007 reported that 78.6% of respondents thought that citizenship ceremonies were an important feature of the day.<sup id="cite_ref-DeeryJagoFredline2007_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeeryJagoFredline2007-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> The official Australia Day Ambassador Program supports celebrations in communities across the nation by facilitating the participation of high-achieving Australians in local community celebrations. In 2011, 385 ambassadors participated in 384 local community celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Australia" title="Order of Australia">Order of Australia</a> awards are also a feature of the day. The Australia Day Achievement Medallion is awarded to citizens by local governments based on excellence in both government and non-government organisations. The governor-general and prime minister both address the nation. On the eve of Australia Day each year, the Prime Minister announces the winner of the Australian of the Year award, presented to an Australian citizen who has shown a "significant contribution to the Australian community and nation" and is an "inspirational role model for the Australian community".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Subcategories of the award include <a href="/wiki/Young_Australian_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Australian of the Year">Young Australian of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senior_Australian_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior Australian of the Year">Senior Australian of the Year</a>, and an award for <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_Local_Hero_Award_recipients" title="List of Australian Local Hero Award recipients">Australia's Local Hero</a>. </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Awards_Announcement_(Australia_Day_Eve,_2005).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg/220px-Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg/330px-Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg/440px-Awards_Announcement_%28Australia_Day_Eve%2C_2005%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1039" data-file-height="788"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Awards_Announcement_(Australia_Day_Eve,_2005).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Awards announcement on Australia Day Eve, 25 January 2005
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day,_Denmark_WA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg/220px-Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg/330px-Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg/440px-Australia_Day%2C_Denmark_WA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Day,_Denmark_WA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Australia Day barbecue at Berridge Park, <a href="/wiki/Denmark,_Western_Australia" title="Denmark, Western Australia">Denmark, Western Australia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Research in 2009 indicated that Australians reflect on history and future fairly equally on Australia Day. Of those polled, 43% agreed that history is the most important thing to think about on Australia Day and 41% said they look towards "our future", while 13% thought it was important to "think about the present at this time" and 3% were unsure.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Despite the date reflecting the arrival of the First Fleet, contemporary celebrations are not particularly historical in their theme. There are no large-scale re-enactments and the national leader's participation is focused largely on events such as the Australian of the Year Awards announcement and Citizenship Ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Possibly reflecting a shift in Australians' understanding of the place of Indigenous Australians in their national identity, <a href="/wiki/Newspoll" title="Newspoll">Newspoll</a> research in November 2009 reported that ninety percent of Australians polled believed "it was important to recognise Australia's indigenous people and culture" as part of Australia Day celebrations. A similar proportion (89%) agreed that "it is important to recognise the cultural diversity of the nation".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Despite the strong attendance at Australia Day events and a positive disposition towards the recognition of Indigenous Australians, the date of the celebrations remains a source of challenge and national discussion. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Change_the_date_movement">Change the date movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Change the date movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australiadayprotest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australiadayprotest.jpg/220px-Australiadayprotest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australiadayprotest.jpg/330px-Australiadayprotest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Australiadayprotest.jpg/440px-Australiadayprotest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="821"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australiadayprotest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An Invasion Day rally in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Some Australians regard Australia Day as a symbol of the adverse impacts of British settlement on Australia's Indigenous peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In 1888, prior to the first centennial anniversary of the First Fleet landing on 26 January 1788, New South Wales premier <a href="/wiki/Henry_Parkes" title="Henry Parkes">Henry Parkes</a> was asked about inclusion of Aboriginal people in the celebrations. He replied: "And remind them that we have robbed them?"<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The celebrations in 1938 were accompanied by an Aboriginal <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Mourning_(Australia)" title="Day of Mourning (Australia)">Day of Mourning</a>. A large gathering of Aboriginal people in Sydney in 1988 led an "Invasion Day" commemoration marking the loss of Indigenous culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Age09_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Age09-7">[7]</a></sup> Some Indigenous figures and others continue to label Australia Day as "Invasion Day", and protests occur almost every year, sometimes at Australia Day events.<sup id="cite_ref-AgeRecon_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgeRecon-59">[59]</a></sup> Thousands of people participate in protest marches in capital cities on Invasion Day/Australia Day; estimates for the 2018 protest in Melbourne range into tens of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The anniversary is also termed by some as "Survival Day" and marked by events such as the Survival Day concert, first held in Sydney in 1992, celebrating the fact that the Indigenous people and culture have survived despite colonisation and discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 2016, <a href="/wiki/National_Indigenous_Television" title="National Indigenous Television">National Indigenous Television</a> chose the name "Survival Day" as its preferred choice on the basis that it acknowledges the mixed nature of the day, saying that the term "recognises the invasion", but does not allow that to frame the entire story of the Aboriginal people.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In response, official celebrations have tried to include Indigenous people, holding ceremonies such as the Woggan-ma-gule ceremony, held in Sydney, which honours the past and celebrates the present.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2017 the council of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Yarra" title="City of Yarra">City of Yarra</a>, a local government of Melbourne, resolved unanimously that it would no longer refer to 26 January as Australia Day and would cease to hold citizenship ceremonies on that day; an event acknowledging Aboriginal culture and history was to be held instead.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Darebin" title="City of Darebin">City of Darebin</a> later followed suit. The federal government immediately deprived the councils of their powers to hold citizenship ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Byron_Shire_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Byron Shire Council">Byron Shire Council</a> became the third council to have its power to have citizenship ceremonies stripped.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 January 2019, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Scott_Morrison" title="Scott Morrison">Scott Morrison</a> announced that, with effect from Australia Day 2020, all local councils would be required to hold citizenship ceremonies on and only on 26 January and 17 September; there would also be a dress code, banning thongs and board shorts.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Crowds estimated as high as 80,000 turned out in an "Invasion Day" protest in Melbourne alone in 2019, and rallies were held across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-SBSInvasion2019_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSInvasion2019-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 12 November 2019, following an online survey, the <a href="/wiki/Inner_West_Council" title="Inner West Council">Inner West Council</a> became the first local authority in Sydney to end Australia Day celebrations, encouraging residents instead to attend the Aboriginal Yabun festival held on that day. The council will still hold a citizenship ceremony on that day.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 23 February 2021, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Mitcham" title="City of Mitcham">City of Mitcham</a> became the first local Council in SA to vote to officially oppose the date of Australia Day. Mayor Dr Holmes-Ross said she felt “comfortable with the council holding events on Australia Day, but I don’t feel comfortable with the date of Australia Day”.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suggested_changes_to_the_date">Suggested changes to the date</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Suggested changes to the date">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_(49791385558).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg/220px-Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg/330px-Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg/440px-Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_%2849791385558%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5168" data-file-height="3448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Invasion_Day_Rally_-_Melbourne_2020_(49791385558).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2020 Invasion Day rally in Melbourne.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Both before the establishment of Australia Day as the national day of Australia, and in the years after its creation, several dates have been proposed for its celebration and, at various times, the possibility of moving Australia Day to an alternative date has been mooted. Some reasons put forward are that the current date, celebrating the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_New_South_Wales" title="Colony of New South Wales">Colony of New South Wales</a>, lacks national significance;<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup> that the day falls during school holidays which limits the engagement of schoolchildren in the event;<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup> and that it fails to encompass members of the indigenous community and some others who perceive the day as commemorating the date of an invasion of their land.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup> Connected to this is the suggestion that moving the date would be seen as a significant symbolic act.<sup id="cite_ref-Nicholson2009-12-29_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholson2009-12-29-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Amongst those calling for change have been <a href="/wiki/Tony_Beddison" title="Tony Beddison">Tony Beddison</a>, then chairman of the Australia Day Committee (Victoria), who argued for change and requested debate on the issue in 1999;<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mick_Dodson" title="Mick Dodson">Mick Dodson</a>, Australian of the Year in 2009, who called for debate as to when Australia Day was held.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC2009-01-26-Dodson_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC2009-01-26-Dodson-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Such a move would have to be made by a combination of the Australian Federal and State Governments,<sup id="cite_ref-Day1999-12-09_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Day1999-12-09-80">[80]</a></sup> and has lacked sufficient political and public support. In 2001 Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> stated that he acknowledged Aboriginal concerns with the date, but that it was nevertheless a significant day in Australia's history, and thus he was in favour of retaining the current date. He also noted that 1 January, which was being discussed in light of the Centenary of Federation, was inappropriate as it coincided with New Year's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodda2001-01-27_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodda2001-01-27-81">[81]</a></sup> In 2009 Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Rudd" title="Kevin Rudd">Kevin Rudd</a> gave a "straightforward no" to a change of date, speaking in response to Mick Dodson's suggestion to reopen the debate. The Opposition Leader, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Turnbull" title="Malcolm Turnbull">Malcolm Turnbull</a>, echoed Rudd's support of 26 January, but, along with Rudd, supported the right of Australians to raise the issue. At the State level, New South Wales Premier <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Rees" title="Nathan Rees">Nathan Rees</a> stated that he was yet to hear a "compelling argument" to support change; and Queensland Premier <a href="/wiki/Anna_Bligh" title="Anna Bligh">Anna Bligh</a> expressed her opposition to a change.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC2009-01-26-Rudd_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC2009-01-26-Rudd-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2017 the annual National General Assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Local_Government_Association" title="Australian Local Government Association">Australian Local Government Association</a> voted (by a majority of 64–62) for councils to consider how to lobby the federal government for a date change.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polling">Polling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Polling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2004, a Newspoll poll that asked if the date of Australia Day should be moved to one that is not associated with European settlement found 79% of respondents favoured no change, 15% favoured change, and 6% were uncommitted.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Blainey" title="Geoffrey Blainey">Geoffrey Blainey</a> said in 2012 that he believed 26 January worked well as Australia Day and that it was at that time more successful than it had ever been.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A January 2017 poll conducted by McNair yellowSquares for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> found that 68% of Australians felt positive about Australia Day, 19% were indifferent and 7% had mixed feelings, with 6% feeling negative about Australia Day. Among Indigenous Australians, however, only 23% felt positive about Australia Day, 31% were negative and 30% had mixed feelings, with 54% favouring a change of date.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_2017-01-26_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_2017-01-26-9">[9]</a></sup> A September 2017 poll conducted by Essential Polling for <i>The Guardian</i> found that 54% were opposed to changing the date; 26% of Australians supported changing the date and 19% had no opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Federation_Pavillion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Federation_Pavillion.jpg/220px-Federation_Pavillion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/Federation_Pavillion.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="267"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Federation_Pavillion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Federation Pavilion, Centennial Park, Sydney, 1 January 1901
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A poll conducted by progressive public policy think tank <a href="/wiki/The_Australia_Institute" title="The Australia Institute">The Australia Institute</a> in 2018 found that 56% do not mind what day it is held.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The same poll found that 49% believe that the date should not be on a date that is offensive to Indigenous Australians, but only 37% believed the current date was offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to Australia day 2019, the conservative public policy think tank <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Public_Affairs" title="Institute of Public Affairs">Institute of Public Affairs (IPA)</a> released a poll that 75% of Australians wanted the date to stay, and the new right wing group Advance Australia's poll had support at 71%, although both groups asked questions about pride in being Australian prior to the headline question.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Social Research Centre, a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_University" title="Australian National University">Australian National University</a>, also released a report in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-90">[90]</a></sup> Their survey found that, when respondents know that 26 January is the anniversary of the arrival of the First Fleet at <a href="/wiki/Port_Jackson" title="Port Jackson">Port Jackson</a>, 70% believe it is the best date for Australia Day, and 27% believe it is not. The report includes demographic factors which affect people's response, such as age, level of education, and state or territory of residence. Those who did not support 26 January as the best date then indicated their support for an alternate date. The three most supported dates were 27 May, 1 January and 8 May. </p>
      <p>Polling by Essential Media since 2015 suggests that the number of people celebrating Australia Day is declining, indicating a shift in attitudes. In 2019 40% celebrated the day, in 2020 34%, and in 2021 it was down to 29% of over 1000 people surveyed. In 2021, 53% said that they are treating the day as just a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-news.com-poll-shock_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.com-poll-shock-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A poll by Ipsos conducted in 2021 found that a majority of Australians either supported or were neutral towards changing the date, with 28% in support and 24% neutral, compared to 48% who did not support changing the date.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> 49% believed that the date would change within the next decade and 41% believed that selecting a new date would improve the lives of Indigenous Australians. Results were split by demographic factors, with age being a significant factor. 47% of people aged 18–24 supported changing the date, compared to only 19% among those aged 55 years or older. Individuals who voted for the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Greens" title="Australian Greens">Greens</a> were most likely to support the date at 67%, followed by <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor</a> voters at 31% and <a href="/wiki/Coalition_(Australia)" title="Coalition (Australia)">Coalition</a> voters at 23%. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suggested_alternative_dates">Suggested alternative dates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Suggested alternative dates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Federation of Australia (1 January)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        As early as 1957, 1 January was suggested as a possible alternative day, to commemorate the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">Federation of Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-almanac_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-almanac-93">[93]</a></sup> In 1902, the year after Federation, 1 January was named "Commonwealth Day".<sup id="cite_ref-ageday_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ageday-94">[94]</a></sup> However, New Year's Day was already a public holiday, and Commonwealth Day did not gather much support.<sup id="cite_ref-ageday_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ageday-94">[94]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Federation of Australia 1901 alternative date (19 January)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        Proposed as an alternative because it is only one week earlier than Australia Day and can represent the year of Federation 19.01.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Act_1986.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Australia_Act_1986.jpg/260px-Australia_Act_1986.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Australia_Act_1986.jpg/390px-Australia_Act_1986.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Australia_Act_1986.jpg/520px-Australia_Act_1986.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="543"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_Act_1986.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Photo of the Australia Act 1986 (United Kingdom) document located in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Canberra" title="Parliament House, Canberra">Parliament House, Canberra</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Independence day (3 March)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        There has been support for an independence day, 3 March, to represent the enacting of the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Act_1986" title="Australia Act 1986">Australia Act 1986</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Anzac Day (25 April)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        There has been a degree of support by some in recent years for making <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Day" title="Anzac Day">Anzac Day</a>, 25 April, Australia's national day, including in 1999, by <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Hollingworth" title="Peter Hollingworth">Peter Hollingworth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantyne2009-12-05_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantyne2009-12-05-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Day1999-12-09_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Day1999-12-09-80">[80]</a></sup> In 2001, following comments made during a review into the future of Anzac Day,<sup id="cite_ref-Stewart2001-04-14_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart2001-04-14-98">[98]</a></sup> the idea of a merger was strongly opposed by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> and Opposition Leader <a href="/wiki/Kim_Beazley" title="Kim Beazley">Kim Beazley</a>, who clarified his earlier position.<sup id="cite_ref-HobartMercury2001-04-26_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HobartMercury2001-04-26-99">[99]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Mate (8 May)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        Starting 2017, there has been a partly serious suggestion to move Australia day to 8 May. This is primarily because of the <a href="/wiki/Homophone" title="Homophone">homophonous</a> quality between "May 8" and the Australian idiom "<a href="/wiki/Mateship" title="Mateship">mate</a>", but also because the opening of the first Federal Parliament was on 9 May.<sup id="cite_ref-News.com.au2017-1-26_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-News.com.au2017-1-26-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CourierMail2017-1-12_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CourierMail2017-1-12-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-May8_–_The_New_Australia_Day_Mate!_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-May8_–_The_New_Australia_Day_Mate!-102">[102]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliamenthouse2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Parliamenthouse2.jpg/300px-Parliamenthouse2.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Parliamenthouse2.jpg/450px-Parliamenthouse2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/Parliamenthouse2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="481" data-file-height="207"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliamenthouse2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Opening of Parliament House in May 1927
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Opening of the first Federal Parliament (9 May)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        The date 9 May is also sometimes suggested, the date on which the first Federal Parliament was opened in Melbourne in 1901, the date of the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Parliament_House,_Canberra" title="Old Parliament House, Canberra">Provisional Parliament House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a> in 1927, and the date of the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Canberra" title="Parliament House, Canberra">New Parliament House</a> in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-SMH2002-01-26_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMH2002-01-26-103">[103]</a></sup> The date has, at various times, found support from former Queensland Premier <a href="/wiki/Peter_Beattie" title="Peter Beattie">Peter Beattie</a>, Tony Beddison,<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup> and Geoffrey Blainey.<sup id="cite_ref-Hudson2001-05-10_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hudson2001-05-10-104">[104]</a></sup> However, the date has been seen by some as being too closely connected with Victoria,<sup id="cite_ref-Turner2000-01-26_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner2000-01-26-105">[105]</a></sup> and its location close to the start of winter has been described as an impediment.<sup id="cite_ref-SMH2002-01-26_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMH2002-01-26-103">[103]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Anniversary of the 1967 referendum (27 May)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        The anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_referendum,_1967_(Aboriginals)" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian referendum, 1967 (Aboriginals)">1967 referendum</a> to amend the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Australia" title="Constitution of Australia">federal constitution</a> has also been suggested.<sup id="cite_ref-Nicholson2009-12-29_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholson2009-12-29-78">[78]</a></sup> The amendments enabled the federal parliament to legislate with regard to Indigenous Australians and allowed for Indigenous Australians to be included in the national census. The public vote in favour was 91%.
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Acceptance of the Constitution (9 July)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        This is the date when Queen Victoria accepted the Constitution of Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-90">[90]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Wattle Day (1 September)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Wattle_Day" title="Wattle Day">Wattle Day</a> is the first day of spring in the southern hemisphere. Australia's <a href="/wiki/Green_and_gold" class="mw-redirect" title="Green and gold">green and gold</a> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Acacia_pycnantha" title="Acacia pycnantha">wattle</a>, and it has symbolised Australia since the early 1800s. Wattle Day has been proposed as the new date for Australia Day since the 1990s and is supported by the National Wattle Day Association.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Tenterfield Oration (24 October)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        "A more meaningful day is October 24, when in 1889 Sir <a href="/wiki/Henry_Parkes" title="Henry Parkes">Henry Parkes</a>, the "Father of Federation", gave his pivotal <a href="/wiki/Tenterfield_Oration" title="Tenterfield Oration">speech at Tenterfield</a> in NSW, which set the course for federation."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eureka_Slaughter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Eureka_Slaughter.jpg/220px-Eureka_Slaughter.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Eureka_Slaughter.jpg/330px-Eureka_Slaughter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Eureka_Slaughter.jpg/440px-Eureka_Slaughter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eureka_Slaughter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Eureka Slaughter</i> by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Doudiet" title="Charles Doudiet">Charles Doudiet</a> (1854).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Eureka Stockade (3 December)
       </dt> 
       <dd>
        The <a href="/wiki/Eureka_Stockade" class="mw-redirect" title="Eureka Stockade">Eureka Stockade</a> on 3 December has had a long history as an alternative choice for Australia Day, having been proposed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bulletin_(Australian_periodical)" title="The Bulletin (Australian periodical)">The Bulletin</a></i> in the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-Hirst2008-01-26_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hirst2008-01-26-109">[109]</a></sup> The Eureka uprising occurred in 1854 during the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_gold_rush" title="Victorian gold rush">Victorian gold rush</a>, and saw a failed rebellion by the miners against the Victorian colonial government. Although the rebellion was crushed, it led to significant reforms, and has been described as being the birthplace of Australian democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Macgregor2004-11-29_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macgregor2004-11-29-110">[110]</a></sup> Supporters of the date have included senator <a href="/wiki/Don_Chipp" title="Don Chipp">Don Chipp</a> and former Victorian Premier <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bracks" title="Steve Bracks">Steve Bracks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballantine1999-12-05_77-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballantine1999-12-05-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DailyTelegraph1999-12-06_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyTelegraph1999-12-06-111">[111]</a></sup> However, the idea has been opposed by both hard-left unions and right-wing nationalist groups, both of whom claim symbolic attachment to the event,<sup id="cite_ref-Macgregor2004-11-29_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macgregor2004-11-29-110">[110]</a></sup> and by some who see it as an essentially Victorian event.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner2000-01-26_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner2000-01-26-105">[105]</a></sup>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
